commit cc0d586f8b5b76ff6d204d7a398541fa166b5e97
Author: Daniel R. Grayson <dan@math.uiuc.edu>
Date:   Thu Dec 24 16:00:05 2015 -0600

    update for Coq v8.5 and primitive projections
    
    We update to the lastest Coq v8.5 commit, and we take into account this
    announcement from the Coq CHANGES file:
    
        - The command "Record foo ..." does not generate induction
          principles (foo_rect, foo_rec, foo_ind) anymore by
          default (feature wish #2693). The command "Variant foo ..." does
          not either. A flag "Set/Unset Nonrecursive Elimination Schemes"
          allows changing this.  The tactic "induction" on a "Record" or a
          "Variant" is now actually doing "destruct".
    
    and change our definition of "total2" back to use "Inductive" instead of
    "Record", thereby avoiding the use of "match" in our master branch.
    (The command "Set Nonrecursive Elimination Schemes" does get
    "total2_rect" defined again, but it doesn't get it used by "induction"
    yet.)

commit 925d9e97903e83d874fc3caf02f631e835831ff5
Author: Daniel R. Grayson <dan@math.uiuc.edu>
Date:   Tue Dec 22 09:08:04 2015 -0600

    Update coq to latest
    
    We update Coq to the latest 8.5 version after the announcement of
    v8.5 RC 1.
    
    This update implements "simple refine", which is the recommended way to
    get the new behavior of the "refine" tactic, so we replace "unshelve
    refine" by "simple refine" everywhere except in those cases where it
    doesn't work.  (It was just a few days ago that we had to replace almost
    all of our uses of "refine" by "unshelve refine".)

commit 2f8a80e4cd2ad1fa5d66a20c5561936fff81f8c5
Author: Daniel R. Grayson <dan@math.uiuc.edu>
Date:   Wed Dec 16 09:41:58 2015 -0500

    [colimits]: add a few lemmas, one failing
    
    The one without a trivial proof is this:
    
    Lemma functorBinarySum_map_eqn {B C:Precategory} (sum : hasBinarySums C)
          (F G F' G' : [B,C]) (p:F→F') (q:G→G') (b:B) :
      binarySumMap_2 (functorBinarySum sum F G) (functorBinarySum sum F' G') p q ◽ b
      =
      binarySumMap_2 (sum (F ◾ b) (G ◾ b)) (sum (F' ◾ b) (G' ◾ b)) (p ◽ b) (q ◽ b).
    
    This failure might be what prevents using this framework with
    SubstitutionSystems on the branch "colimits". Since
    [functorBinaryProduct_map_eqn] admits a trivial proof, that's an argument for
    replacing the proof of functorBinarySum by one that's parallel to the proof of
    functorBinaryProduct, rather than deducing it as a corollary.  Maybe then we
    could also write [universalObject sum] instead of [rm_opp_ob (universalObject
    sum)]

    introduce isdectotal and isdeccotrans
    
    Definition isdectotal { X : UU } ( R : hrel X ) := ∀ x1 x2 , R x1 x2 ⨿ R x2 x1 .
    Definition isdeccotrans { X : UU } ( R : hrel X ) := ∀ x1 x2 x3 , R x1 x3 -> R x1 x2 ⨿ R x2 x3 .

    relate isolated points to complementary pairs

    Definition isaprop_isolation {X:UU} (x:X) (is:isisolated X x) (y:X) : isaprop (isolation x is y)
    Definition isolation_to_inequality {X:UU} (x:X) (is:isisolated X x) (y:X) : isolation x is y -> x ≠ y
    Definition inequality_to_isolation {X:UU} (x:X) (is:isisolated X x) (y:X) : x ≠ y -> isolation x is y

commit fe31b05f188eec9ae598079f3e862407e93bbab8
Author: Daniel R. Grayson <dan@math.uiuc.edu>
Date:   Tue Nov 3 08:24:50 2015 -0500

    found an even better definition of isdecprop
    
    ... namely:
    
      Definition isdecprop (P:UU) := isaprop P × (P ⨿ ¬P).
    
    Showing that isdecprop(P) is a proposition will be done with funextfun.
    
    We avoid asserting contractibility of P ⨿ ¬P because that can only be proven
    with the aid of funextempty.
    
    We avoid providing a replacement proposition for ¬P as part of the data,
    because then isdecprop(P) is in a higher universe, and because we can easily
    get a new proposition Q logically equivalent to ¬P:
    
      Definition neg_decprop {P} (i: isdecprop P) := Σ n:¬P, ii2 n = pr2 i.
    
    Proving Q is a proposition will not use funextempty, because it will depend
    only on ii2 being an inclusion:
    
      Lemma isaprop_neg_decprop {P} (i:isdecprop P) : isaprop (neg_decprop i).
        (to be proven)
    
    Proving the logical equivalence will:
    
      Lemma neg_decprop_negates {P} (i:isdecprop P) : neg_decprop i <-> ¬ P.

      (Σ i, X i) ≃ (Σ (i:stn n), X (dni _ (lastelement _) i)) ⨿ X (lastelement _).
    
    The issue is that we would like one of the homotopy equivalences
    associated with weqdnicoprod, which proves stn n ⨿ unit ≃ stn (S n), to
    give refl more often:
    
          idpath (● 0) = ! homotweqinvweq (weqdnicoprod 1 (lastelement 1)) (● 0)

commit 1ba69a3214c187bafa51fe1608db9238abd74eab
Author: Daniel R. Grayson <dan@math.uiuc.edu>
Date:   Mon Oct 26 13:20:49 2015 -0400

    renaming total2_paths_second_isaprop ..., part 1
    
    and introducing these:
    
     Definition isPredicate {X} (Y : X->UU) := ∀ x, isaprop (Y x).
    
     Theorem subtype_Injectivity {A : UU} (B : A -> UU) :
       isPredicate B -> ∀ (x y : total2 B), (x = y) ≃ (pr1 x = pr1 y).
    
     Corollary subtype_equality (A : UU) (B : A -> UU) (is : forall a, isaprop (B a))
        (s s' : total2 (fun x => B x)) : pr1 s = pr1 s' -> s = s'.
    
     Definition subtype_pair_equality {X} {P:X -> UU} (is: isPredicate P)
                {x y:X} {p:P x} {q:P y} :
       x = y -> (x,,p) = (y,,q).

commit 63ee00eac6e8537e4425844a7da982063668f30e
Author: Daniel R. Grayson <dan@math.uiuc.edu>
Date:   Sun Oct 25 10:02:49 2015 -0400

    abstract a lemma from Vladimir's proof of fincard
    
    Here is the lemma:
    
        Definition squash_pairs_to_set {Y} (F:Y->UU) :
          (isaset Y) -> (∀ y y', F y -> F y' -> y=y') ->
          (∃ y, F y) -> Y.
    
    We also provide this generalization:
    
          Definition squash_to_set {X Y} (is:isaset Y) (f:X->Y) :
              (∀ x x', f x = f x') -> ∥ X ∥ -> Y.
    
    The new proof of fincard is short:
    
        Definition fincard { X : UU } ( is : isfinite X ) : nat .
        Proof.
          intros. apply (squash_pairs_to_set (λ n, stn n ≃ X) isasetnat).
          { intros n n' w w'. apply weqtoeqstn. exact (invweq w' ∘ w)%weq. }
          assumption.
        Defined.
    
    An application of the generalization is to existence of finite sums:
    
       Definition finsum {X} (fin : isfinite X) (f : X -> nat) : nat.
    
    My old proof was more complicated.

commit 4444edc6da1cce19b7dd2f3a480a72320cb28182
Author: Daniel R. Grayson <dan@math.uiuc.edu>
Date:   Wed Jul 1 16:56:54 2015 -0400

    update coq, encounter bug
    
    The coq release we update to here concerns assumption printing, and
    causes our single use of assumption printing to go into an infinite
    loop:
    
        "sub/coq/bin/coqc"  -q  -R "UniMath" UniMath  -indices-matter -type-in-type  UniMath/Ktheory/Circle
        Fetching opaque proofs from disk for UniMath.Foundations.Generalities.uu0d
        make: *** [UniMath/Ktheory/Circle.vo] Cputime limit exceeded: 24
    
    To demonstrate the problem, simply run
    
           ulimit -t 60
           make
    
    Compare with the previous release.
    To clean up first, if necessary, run
    
           make git-clean
    
    Here's the commit message for the coq commit that broke it:
    
        commit 2defd4c15467736b73f69adb501e3a4fe2111ce5
        Author: Enrico Tassi <Enrico.Tassi@inria.fr>
        Date:   Mon Jun 29 21:30:19 2015 +0200
    
            Assumptions: more informative print for False axiom (Close: #4054)
    
            When an axiom of an empty type is matched in order to inhabit
            a type, do print that type (as if each use of that axiom was a
            distinct foo_subproof).
    
            E.g.
    
              Lemma w : True.
              Proof. case demon. Qed.
    
              Lemma x y : y = 0 /\ True /\ forall w, w = y.
              Proof. split. case demon. split; [ exact w | case demon ]. Qed.
    
              Print Assumptions x.
    
            Prints:
    
              Axioms:
              demon : False
               used in x to prove: forall w : nat, w = y
               used in w to prove: True
               used in x to prove: y = 0

commit b81f31d924d4d55cbeadf0eab51a816d6c82b6fb
Author: Alex Kavvos <alex.kavvos@cs.ox.ac.uk>
Date:   Sat Dec 13 23:25:34 2014 +0000

    Further overhauling.
    
    There is only one substantial change: to deal with weak
    equivalences, we introduce a function which, for each weak
    equivalence and point in the codomain, gives the hfiber that is
    the centre of contraction, of type
    
    Definition weqccontrhfiber {X Y : UU} (w : weq X Y) (y : Y) : hfiber w y.
    
    and a function which, for the same data, gives a proof of equality
    of anything in the hfiber to this centre of contraction, of type
    
    Definition weqccontrhfiber2 {X Y : UU} (w : weq X Y) (y : Y) :
      forall x : hfiber w y, x = weqccontrhfiber w y.

    change MAKEFILES to UMAKEFILES
    
    It turns out that setting MAKEFILES has a disastrous effect,
    since the variable is used by "make" and is passed onward
    during recursive invocations.  This explains the strange
    bug discussed in previous commits.

      T0 := trivialTorsor ℤ : Torsor ℤ
      Y : Type
      y : Y
      l : y == y
      ============================
       ap pr1
         (proofirrGuidedHomotopy T0 (confun T0 y) (confun T0 l)
            (makeGuidedHomotopy2 (confun T0 y) (confun T0 l))
            (makeGuidedHomotopy2 (confun T0 y) (confun T0 l))) ==
       idpath y

commit 0944a810986f5a352ce07dbd0d4e5d5b4d7230e5
Author: Daniel R. Grayson <dan@math.uiuc.edu>
Date:   Sat Mar 29 17:53:41 2014 -0400

    ZZTorsorRecursionEquiv with computation rule
    
    Definition ZZTorsorRecursionEquiv {T:Torsor ZZ} (P:T->Type)
          (IH:forall t, weq (P t) (P (one + t))) :
      forall t0,
      weq (total2 (fun
              f:forall t, P t =>
                forall t, f (one + t) == IH t (f t)))
          (P t0).

commit c91b95c7eb1d683cd60bb11c651b4bf4567050d6
Author: Daniel R. Grayson <dan@math.uiuc.edu>
Date:   Sat Mar 29 17:45:17 2014 -0400

    proved ZZBiRecursionEquiv, with computation rule
    
    Definition ZZBiRecursionEquiv (P:ZZ->Type) (IH :forall i, weq (P i) (P(1+i))) :
      weq (total2 (ZZBiRecursionData P IH)) (P 0).

    uniqueness lemma for nat
    
    Lemma uniqueness (P:nat->Type) (p0:P 0) (IH:forall n, P n->P(S n)) :
        iscontr (total2 (fun f:forall n, P n =>
                           dirprod (f 0==p0) (forall n, f(S n)==IH n (f n)))).

commit 614be94638df02c5233ea3667ad353aa590f82b6
Author: Daniel R. Grayson <dan@math.uiuc.edu>
Date:   Mon Jan 27 13:37:43 2014 -0500

    add a lemma about representations of functors
    
      Lemma representingIso {C} (X:C==>SET) (r:Representation X) :
        forall d:ob C,
          isweq (fun p : Hom (representingObject r) d => (#X p) (representingElement r)).
    
    The proof is short:
    
      Proof. intros. intros y. exact (representingInitiality r (d,,y)). Qed.

commit 3a190ed2247aa265f31fa5cfc0dd855354985df2
Author: Daniel R. Grayson <dan@math.uiuc.edu>
Date:   Thu Dec 5 16:55:40 2013 -0500

    Declare precategory_id_comp to take values in UU
    
    Unfortunately, total2, and hence dirprod, take values in
    Type, and thus certain uses of "destruct" don't work
    because UU and Type don't match.
    
    A better fix would be to declare total2 to take values
    in UU, but that breaks some coercions, because UU is
    not a "SortClass".

commit 736d9f71494c64b4232822452d8cfbf4b1ec39f4
Author: Vladimir Voevodsky <vladimir@ias.edu>
Date:   Wed Nov 6 16:17:34 2013 -0500

    New material added and small changes made.
    
    The only two changes which may affect the behavior of the library in the files compatible with its Nov. 6, 2011 version are as follows:
    
    1. The arguments of the notation "ct" (file hSet.v) have changed. The arguments now are "( R , is , x , y )" where "R" is a relation on an hSet "T",  "is" a proof that "R" is decidable and "x" and "y" are objects of "X" such that "R x y" holds. The previous version required "is" to be a part of a canonical structure on "R" and used Georges Gonthier trick of phantom types.
    
    2. The name of the lemma "plusminusnmm" (file hnat.v) is changed to "minusplusnmm" (since it better confirms with the naming convenion and since another lemma with the name "plusminusnmm" was added).
    
    Other chnages which should not affect the behavior of the library with existing files are as follows:
    
    3. Some changes had to be made in order to ensure that all the files of the library continue working if "total2" is introduced as "Inductive" instead of as "Record". In particular all the uses of canonical structures are removed from the library itself. However, "total2" is still defined through "Record" to make it possible for the users of the library to use canonical structures.
    
    4. A number of simple lemmas were added to hnat.v especially in connection with the behavior of "minus" on natural numbers. This is being done in order to add in a more systematic way some of the results required for the development of the p-adic numbers.

commit 42d0d397fbf5704e6eda03efebe5f5e2422837a6
Author: Daniel R. Grayson <dan@math.uiuc.edu>
Date:   Wed Nov 6 13:33:06 2013 -0500

    comment out the recently added lines  Add LoadPath ".." as Foundations
    
    The reason is that the path is relative, but not relative to the directory
    containing the source file, but rather, relative to the current working
    directory of the compiler.  This can cause confusion if a sibling to the top
    level directory of this repository happens to be called "Foundations", because
    coq_makefile generates compilation commands that are run in the top level
    directory.

commit aadd0e80875f084185484c823f39fe2dd6965851
Author: Daniel R. Grayson <dan@math.uiuc.edu>
Date:   Sat Nov 2 17:18:22 2013 -0400

    add loadpath commands for interactive "Foundations" access
    
    Now that we are using fully qualified library names, such as
    Foundations.Generalities.uu0, we have to arrange for coqtop to work, especially
    when run by Proof General.  One way would be to give it "-R . Foundations" as
    command line options.  But Proof General has a strange sort of bug that causes
    it to loop forever when starting up coq after you evaluate
    
         (setq coq-prog-args '("-emacs" "-R" "." "Foo"))
    
    .  The best solution seems to be to add lines
    
          Add LoadPath ".." as Foundations.
    
    to our *.v source files, which we do in this commit.

commit 5a198f77730617c71686ab83184b49472b5c29ea
Author: Daniel R. Grayson <dan@math.uiuc.edu>
Date:   Wed Oct 30 13:11:00 2013 -0400

    Reorganize to work will with coq_makefile
    
    Now the *.v files are all in the subdirectory Foundations, and "make install"
    will install them in the directory user-contrib/Foundations inside the
    currently running coqc distribution tree.
    
    Instead of using coq_makefile to make the file "Makefile", we use it to make
    the file "Make.makefile".  That way we have a Makefile we can edit manually,
    which is convenient, for example, for making a TAGS file.

commit fefe484a302a2d30b95996b4e471defff5ef87cf
Author: Daniel R. Grayson <dan@math.uiuc.edu>
Date:   Wed Oct 30 11:13:05 2013 -0400

    Reorganize the files into two subdirectories
    
    This will make it possible for the Rezk Completion files to be used with
    another version of the Foundations files of Voevodsky.  (The problem is that
    coq doesn't like to find a file such as 'uuu.v' occurring twice in directories
    of the search path.)  The advantages are: that a developer of the Foundations
    files can easily verify that the Rezk Completion proof continues works; and
    that a developer of a subsequent proof can incorporate all of the Foundations
    files as well as the Rezk Completion proof.
    
    Comments have been inserted into the file 'Make' to illustrate an alternative
    usage.
